gpg --list-keys
gpg --list-secret-keys
gpg --armor --export [your\_email@example.com](mailto:your_email@example.com) > publickey.asc
gpg --import publickey.asc
gpg --encrypt --recipient [recipient\_email@example.com](mailto:recipient_email@example.com) file.txt
gpg --output file.txt --decrypt file.txt.gpg
gpg --symmetric file.txt
gpg --output file.txt --decrypt file.txt.gpg
gpg --clearsign file.txt
gpg --verify file.txt.asc
gpg --encrypt --sign --recipient [recipient\_email@example.com](mailto:recipient_email@example.com) file.txt
gpg --output file.txt --decrypt file.txt.gpg
* You must trust the public key you import. Use gpg --edit-key and the trust command to set the trust level.
* You can delete keys with gpg --delete-key and gpg --delete-secret-key.

ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt - Basic directory brute-force
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/admin/FUZZ -w admin_panels.txt - Brute-force admin paths
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/page.php?file=FUZZ -w wordlist.txt - Parameter fuzzing
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -mc 200 - Filter only 200 OK responses
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -fc 403 - Filter out 403 Forbidden
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -t 50 - Increase threads to 50
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -e .php,.html,.txt - Add extensions
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -r - Follow redirects
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -o results.json -of json - Output to JSON
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -o results.html -of html - Output to HTML
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -recursion - Recursive fuzzing
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -recursion-depth 3 - Limit recursion depth
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -H "User-Agent: Mozilla" - Custom header
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w common.txt -H "X-Api-Key: FUZZ" - Header fuzzing
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/login -X POST -d "user=admin&pass=FUZZ" -w passwords.txt - POST data fuzzing
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/search.php?q=FUZZ -w wordlist.txt - URL parameter fuzzing
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -fs 4242 - Filter by response size
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -fw 25 - Filter by response words
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -fl 12 - Filter by response lines
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -ac - Automatically calibrate filters
ffuf: ffuf -request request.txt -w wordlist.txt - Use raw request file
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -maxtime 300 - Limit total scan time to 5 minutes
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -rate 100 - Throttle to 100 requests/sec
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -mc all - Show all status codes
ffuf: ffuf -u http://example.com/FUZZ -w wordlist.txt -p 0.1 - Add 100ms delay between requests

# Connect to a device over TCP/IP
adb connect <device_ip>:5555
# Disconnect from a device
adb disconnect <device_ip>:5555
# List connected devices
adb devices
# Start a shell on the device
adb shell
# Push a file to the device
adb push <local_file> <remote_path>
# Pull a file from the device
adb pull <remote_file> <local_path>
# Reboot the device
adb reboot
# Install an APK
adb install <apk_file>
# Uninstall an app
adb uninstall <package_name>
# Copy file using shell
adb shell cp <source> <destination>
# Remove a file on the device
adb shell rm <file_path>
# Remount file system as read-write
adb remount
# Logcat (view device logs)
adb logcat
# Restart adb server
adb kill-server
adb start-server
#lists all the commands we can use on adb.
adb 
#lists the emulators currently active on the computer.
adb devices 
#lists all application packages. 
adb shell pm list packages 
#extract the apk file from the emulator to the computer
##find target application
adb shell pm list packages | grep exampleApp 
##get the full path name of the APK file for the desired package
adb shell pm path com.exampleApp
##get apk to the computer
adb pull /data/app/com.exampleApp/base.apk /<target directory on computer>
#install the apk on emulator
adb install example.apk 
#connect&run commands on multiple emulator
adb -s IP:PORT <command>

sgpt switches:
sgpt --repl    Start an interactive REPL (Read-Eval-Print Loop) chatbot mode. Useful for ongoing conversations.            
sgpt --shell   Generate shell commands based on the prompt. Outputs raw shell commands.                                    
sgpt --code    Generate code (any language) based on your prompt. Outputs raw code.                                        
sgpt --chat    Use conversation mode to maintain context across multiple messages (better in interactive chat scenarios).  
sgpt --explain Explain the command or code that you provide.                                                               
sgpt --python  Generate Python code only (forces code completion to Python language).                                      
sgpt --execute     Executes the generated shell command automatically. Use with caution.
sgpt --no-cache    Disable caching of responses.                                        
sgpt --debug       Enable verbose/debug mode — see the raw API calls, tokens used, etc. 
sgpt --model MODEL_NAME   Specify which OpenAI model to use (e.g.  gpt-4o ,  gpt-4 ,  gpt-3.5-turbo ).  
sgpt --temperature        Set randomness/creativity of output (0-2; lower = more deterministic).        
sgpt --top-p              Nucleus sampling parameter for controlling diversity.                         
sgpt --input FILE    Read the prompt from a file.                   
sgpt --output FILE   Save the response to a file.                   
sgpt --copy          Automatically copy the response to clipboard.  
sgpt --explain "iptables -A INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -j ACCEPT"

ip n or ip neigh it like arp -a but has nice colors and more details. 
ip a show dev wlan0 (replaced ifconfig) shows interface configuration
ip a add 192.168.1.200/255.255.255.0 dev eth0 (configure ip address full mask per dev)
ip a add 192.168.1.200/24 dev eth0 (configure ip interface with cidr)
ip addr add 192.168.1.50/24 brd + dev eth0 label eth0Home (give the int a nice name)
ip a del 192.168.1.200/24 dev eth0 (remove ip config from interface)
ip n show (display neighbor/router and if routable)
ip a (show general ip address info)
ip -s -s n f 192.168.1.5 (flush your arp table)
ip -s -s n flush 192.168.1.5 (Same as above)
ip a show eth0
ip a list eth0
ip a show dev eth0
ip -4 a (show ipv4)
ip -6 a (show ipv6)
ip r list or ip route list (shows routing table)
ip r list [options] ip route

ip route add {NETWORK/MASK} via {GATEWAYIP} example:
ip route add 192.168.1.0/24 via 192.168.1.254
ip route add {NETWORK/MASK} dev {DEVICE}
## Add default route using ip ##
ip route add default {NETWORK/MASK} dev {DEVICE}
ip route add default {NETWORK/MASK} via {GATEWAYIP}
ip route del default (delete default gateway gw)

Add a plain route to network 192.168.1.0/24 via gateway 192.168.1.254:
ip route add 192.168.1.0/24 via 192.168.1.254
To route all traffic via 192.168.1.254 gateway connected via eth0 network interface:
ip route add 192.168.1.0/24 dev eth0
ip route del default (delete default route)

irssi: /server <hostname> - Connect to a server (e.g., /server irc.libera.chat)
irssi: /connect <hostname> - Alias of /server
irssi: /disconnect - Disconnect from current IRC server
irssi: /quit [message] - Quit IRC with optional message
irssi: /msg NickServ IDENTIFY <your_password> - Identify yourself to NickServ
irssi: /msg NickServ REGISTER <password> <email> - Register your nickname
irssi: /join #channel - Join a channel
irssi: /part [#channel] [message] - Leave a channel
irssi: /topic <new topic> - Set the topic (if you have permission)
irssi: /names - List users in the current channel
irssi: <Enter> - Sends your message
irssi: /msg <nick> <message> - Send private message
irssi: /me <action> - Emote (e.g., /me waves)
irssi: /notice <nick> <message> - Send a notice to user
irssi: /nick <newnick> - Change your nickname
irssi: /whois <nick> - Info about a user
irssi: /whowas <nick> - Info on recently disconnected user
irssi: /kick <nick> [reason] - Kick user (if you're op)
irssi: /ban <nick> - Ban user (if you're op)
irssi: /window list - List all open windows
irssi: /window goto <#> - Go to a specific window
irssi: Alt + # - Switch windows (Alt+2 for window 2)
irssi: /close - Close the current window
irssi: /set autolog on - Enable automatic logging
irssi: /set nick <nickname> - Set default nickname
irssi: /save - Save your current configuration

enum4linux -a target-ip: Do Everything, runs all options apart from dictionary based share name guessing
enum4linux -G target-ip: Lists groups. if the server allows it, you can also specify username -u and password -p
enum4linux -i target-ip: Pull information about printers known to the remove device.
enum4linux -o target-ip: Pulls OS information using smbclient, this can pull the service pack version on some versions of Windows
enum4linux -R 600-660 target-ip: Pull usernames using a custom RID range
enum4linux -r target-ip: Pulls usernames from the default RID range (500-550,1000-1050)
enum4linux -s shares.txt target-ip: Perform a dictionary attack, if the server doesn't let you retrieve a share list
enum4linux -S target-ip: List Windows shares, again you can also specify username -u and password -p
enum4linux -u administrator -p password -U target-ip: If you've managed to obtain credentials, you can pull a full list of users regardless of the RestrictAnonymous option
enum4linux -U target-ip: Lists usernames, if the server allows it - (RestrictAnonymous = 0)
enum4linux -v target-ip: Verbose mode, shows the underlying commands being executed by enum4linux

SBD.exe
sbd is a Netcat-clone, designed to be portable and offer strong encryption. It runs on Unix-like operating systems and on Microsoft Win32. sbd features AES-CBC-128 + HMAC-SHA1 encryption (by Christophe Devine), program execution (-e option), choosing source port, continuous reconnection with delay, and some other nice features. sbd supports TCP/IP communication only. sbd.exe (part of the Kali linux distribution: /usr/share/windows-binaries/backdoors/sbd.exe) can be uploaded to a windows box as a Netcat alternative.
